тАШрдПрддреЗ рдЕрд╕реГрдЧреНрд░рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреГрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рднрд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЬрдорджрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░рд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░рдВ рдкрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╕реЛрдорджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН– рдПрддреЗ рдЕрд╕реГрдЧреНрд░рдВ рдЬрдорджрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

62 (774)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Jamadagni Bh─Бrgava
30 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
Though long, this hymn remains focused on the familiar details of the preparation of the soma, often ennobled by establishing cosmic parallels. The journey across1284 IX.62
the fleece is especially prominent, and the soma is frequently likened to a fast horse. One verse, 17, is more specific than the usual generic treatments: here the soma is a horse yoked to the chariot of the sacrifice, which has three backs and three seats, presumably the three pressings and the three fires, by the visionary thoughts of the seven seers. It is also notable how often Soma is called a poet or connected with poetry in the second part of this hymn (vss. 13, 14, 25, 26, 27, 30). In the final verse he is in fact called тАЬthe entruthed poetтАЭ or тАЬthe poet (who is) truth (itself),тАЭ a power
ful expression of his relationship to creative speech.
Though some of the tr╠еcas display internal formal unity (e.g., vss. 19тАУ21 begin ning with ─Б╠Б), most do not. The poet to whom the hymn is attributed names himself in verse 24.

Jamison Brereton Notes

61-67 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

On the place of these long hymns in the structure of the maс╣Зс╕Нala, see published introduction. to IX.61. All of these hymns consist of collections of tс╣Ыcas of varying degrees of cohesion. In fact, it is surprising how few tс╣Ыcas display a real attempt at thematic or lexical unity, and what they do show is often simply the byproduct of the fact that both the lexicon and thematic preoccupations of Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX are comparatively limited and so similar words and themes are not unlikely to show up in adjacent verses. This lack of unity contrasts, I think (this is my unsystematic and anecdotal impression) with collections of tс╣Ыcas in other maс╣Зс╕Нalas, notably VIII.

English translation:

тАЬPowerful, repelling evils, bestowing happiness and riches upon our sons and horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The prize-seekers, smashing apart the many obstacles to progress, making the ways easy going for our offspring
and for our steed by their own extension,

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. has no finite verb, just two nom. pl. participles. With its nom. pl. subj. it can be dependent on vs. 1 or vs. 3 (or both); I prefer anticipatory dependence on vs. 3 because of the repetition of kс╣Ыс╣Зv├бntaс╕е and the parallel datives.

Note the juxtaposition of the opposites durit─Б╠Бlit. тАШill-goingsтАЩ (p─Бda a) and sug─Б╠Бlit.

тАШgood-goingsтАЩ (p─Бda b), formed with two different verbs of motion (тИЪi, тИЪg─Б). It is difficult to capture this relationship in Engl. without awkwardness, as the literal tr. just given demonstrate.

My tr. follows Geldner in taking ├бrvate parallel to tok─Б╠Бya тАЬfor our offsping and for our steedтАЭ; I am somewhat tempted to take ├бrvate as an anticipatory parallel to g├бve in 3a, with which it forms a more natural class (тАЬmaking wide space for our steed and for our cowтАЭ), but I canтАЩt see how to do that without brutally splitting up 2c, since kс╣Ыс╣Зv├бntaс╕е is required to govern sug─Б╠Бin 2b.

тАЬThe cattle sweeten with their milk the beautiful food that is asked for by the gods; the Soma when effused by the priests is cleansed in the water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The beautiful stalk coveted by the godsтАФ(the soma) rinsed in the waters, pressed by menтАФ
do the cows sweeten with their milk.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The fluent Engl. of the tr. conceals a syntactic problem: soma should be the obj. of the verb sv├бdanti in c, and the first p─Бda, which is entirely in the neuter, with the NP led by ├бndhas-, allows such an acc. interpr. However, the intermediate p─Бda (b) is stubbornly in the masc. nominative (dh┼лt├бс╕е тАж sut├бс╕е). We must either take b as a parenthetical nominal clause, as Geldner and I do, or take ab as entirely in the nominative (as Renou may do - his structure is not entirely clear) as a separate nominal clause, and supply a resumptive pronominal acc. for c.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again no obvious signs of unity, beyond the progress through the preparation of soma. Note, however, that 4b and 5b both begin aps├║ and the opening of 6b, ├б┼Ы┼л(┼Ыubhan) echoes that opening phonologically.

Then, like drivers a horse, they have beautified him for the immortal, the sap of honey for joint revelry. с│У

As drivers deck a courser, so have they adorned the meath’s juice for
Ambrosia, for the festival.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca shows no strong signs of internal unity, save for the тАЬsittingтАЭ found in both 7 and 8, but it does echo some of the material earlier in the hymn: ├бsс╣Ыgram in 7b matches the same verb in 1a; ─Б╠Бsadaс╕е in 7c recalls ─Б╠Бsadat in 4c, while s─л╠Бdan y├│n─Б (8c) is a different echo of 4c y├│nim ─Б╠Бsadat; arс╣гa (8a) picks up arс╣гanti (3b); sv─Б╠Бdiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е in 9b expresses the result of sv├бdanti in 5c; and varivo-v├нd in 9c is a paraphrase of kс╣Ыс╣Зv├бnto v├бrivaс╕е in 2c. Jamison Brereton Notes

The metaphorical universe of the soma hymns makes it difficult to interpr. the phrase ghс╣Ыt├бm p├бyaс╕е, lit. тАЬghee (and) milk.тАЭ In the published translation I take the phrase as the ultimate goal of p├бri srava, referring to the milk with which the soma will be mixed after its trip across the filter. See the esp. explicit IX.31.5 t├║bhyaс╣Г g─Б╠Бvo ghс╣Ыt├бm p├бyah тАж dudhr├й тАЬFor you the cows have milked out ghee and milk,тАЭ which identifies the phrase as referring to substance(s) that the cows produce for soma, real dairy products. But soma is also sometimes compared to milk and to ghee (e.g., IX.74.4), and so the phrase can also be an appositive metaphorically characterizing the subject soma, accounting for GeldnerтАЩs тАЬLaufe du тАж als Schmalz und Milch.тАЭ However, our 5c sv├бdanti g─Б╠Бvo p├бyobhiс╕е тАЬthe cows sweeten (soma) with their milkтАЭ suggests that the milk and ghee in this vs. are likewise firmly bovine

  • though see 20b below.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca shows no strong signs of internal unity, save for the тАЬsittingтАЭ found in both 7 and 8, but it does echo some of the material earlier in the hymn: ├бsс╣Ыgram in 7b matches the same verb in 1a; ─Б╠Бsadaс╕е in 7c recalls ─Б╠Бsadat in 4c, while s─л╠Бdan y├│n─Б (8c) is a different echo of 4c y├│nim ─Б╠Бsadat; arс╣гa (8a) picks up arс╣гanti (3b); sv─Б╠Бdiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е in 9b expresses the result of sv├бdanti in 5c; and varivo-v├нd in 9c is a paraphrase of kс╣Ыс╣Зv├бnto v├бrivaс╕е in 2c. It may also be worth noting that this is the first place in the hymn that the divine recipients of soma are mentioned: ├нndr─Бya 8a, ├бс╣Еgirobhyaс╕е 9b.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis all-seeing Pavam─Бna Soma deposited (in the vessels), sending forth abundant (food), the product of the waters, is known (by all).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Here has the limitless one been established; purifying himself, he takes note of
lofty friendship while being impelled.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Several items in this vs. present choices of interpr., none of which are strongly either favored or disfavored.

The first issue is hit├бс╕е: as often in this maс╣Зс╕Нala (cf. comm. ad IX.1.2, 44.2, etc.), it could belong either to тИЪdh─Б or to тИЪhi. The presence of a verb form belonging undeniably to the latter, hinv─Бn├бс╕е in c, cuts both ways, as the poet could either be reinforcing the sense by duplicate forms of the same root or making a pun utilizing two different roots. In a similar situation in IX.44.2, with hit├бс╕е тАж hinve, I opted to take both to тИЪhi (though not with any emphatic feeling about it), while here I take hit├б- to тИЪdh─Б, as a pun (again, not emphatically). The deciding factor here for me is the deictic demon. ay├бm тАШright hereтАЩ, which may point to the current location of the soma, expressed by тАШestablished, placedтАЩ. Renou also takes it to тИЪdh─Б, but Geldner to тИЪhi.

The other uncertainty in the vs. is how to construe ─Б╠Бpyam bс╣Ыh├бt тАЬlofty friendshipтАЭ: is it the complement of cetati or of hinv─Бn├бс╕е – which brings up the further question of the function of the latter participle. Med. hinv├бte, etc., can either take an obj. or be passive; in particular the part. hinv─Бn├б- is about evenly split. For a nearby pass. form, see, e.g., IX.64.9; for a nearby transitive form, see IX.63.7 hinv─Бn├│ m─Б╠Бnuс╣г─лr ap├бс╕е. Both Geldner and Renou take it as tr.

here (e.g., тАЬdie hohe Freundschaft zur eile treibendтАЭ), while I have chosen to take it as passive and to construe the acc. with cetati, on the grounds that I donтАЩt know what it would mean to тАЬimpel friendshipтАЭ (though such an image is well within the potential range of a RVic poet). Got┼Н (1st class, 139) takes it as I do.

Most active and benevolent, this Pavamana, sent to us
For lofty friendship, meditates.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two vss. contain forms of kav├н-. The epithet тАЬwide-goingтАЭ (urug─Бy├б13c) may be further specified in the phrase vim─Б╠Бno r├бjasaс╕е тАЬmeasurer of the airy realmтАЭ (14b) – in both cases probably a way of giving a cosmic dimension to the journey across the filter. The third vs. (15) does not participate in these commonalities.

Griffith

Wandering far, with wise designs, the juice here present is effused,
Made beautiful by living men.

Geldner

Von den Ayu┬┤s geputzt wird er umgegossen, der Weitschreitende mit dem Sehersinn.

Grassmann

Er ist es, der sich rings ergiesst, gereinigt von den eifrigen, Der weise, weithin schreitende.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two vss. contain forms of kav├н-. The epithet тАЬwide-goingтАЭ (urug─Бy├б13c) may be further specified in the phrase vim─Б╠Бno r├бjasaс╕е тАЬmeasurer of the airy realmтАЭ (14b) – in both cases probably a way of giving a cosmic dimension to the journey across the filter. English translation:

тАЬgenitive rated and praised by song, Indu at this sacrifice is deposited in his plural ce for Indra, like a bird on its nest.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Born on a mountain [/begotten by a hymn], praised here, the drop is placed for Indra,
a bird in his womb, as if in a nest.

Jamison Brereton Notes

gir─Б╠Бj─Бt├бс╕е тАЬborn on a mountainтАЭ is in the first instance a phrasal variant of giriс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Бс╕е тАШmountain-abidingтАЩ in 4b, with gir─Б╠Бshowing the i-stem loc. in -─Б regular before consonants (see, e.g., Lanman, Noun Inflect, 385). This interpr. is followed by Geldner and Renou in their tr. (see also Ober II.13). However, gir─Б╠Бcan also be, as Oldenberg and Geldner (n. 15a) point out, the instr. sg. of g├нr- тАШhymnтАЩ; in fact Grassmann puts it there. The alt. given in the published translation тАЬ[/begotten by a hymn]тАЭ reflects this other possible analysis; that soma is produced to the accompaniment of hymns would make this statement true in ritual logic. It is also possible that gir─Б╠БтАШby a hymnтАЩ could be construed with stut├бс╕е тАШpraisedтАЩ later in the p─Бda. And to make things even more complex, stut├бс╕е might also evoke sut├бс╕е тАШpressedтАЩ.

The pass. dh─лyate in b might weakly support taking hit├бс╕е in 10a to тИЪdh─Б as well.

P─Бda c is the third instantiation (always in the c p─Бda) of the image comparing soma installed in the wooden cups to a bird on a y├│ni-: 4c ┼Ыyen├│ n├б y├│nim ─Б╠Бsadat, 8c s─л╠Бdan y├│n─Б v├бneс╣гv ─Б╠Б, our 15c v├нr y├│n─Б vasat─Б╠Бv iva - and cf. in the preceding hymn IX.61.21c s─л╠Бda├▒ chyen├│ n├б y├│nim ─Б╠Б. Judging from the position of ivain our vs., both the bird and the y├│nihave become so much part of the identity of soma that only the тАШnestтАЩ (vasat├н-) is considered part of the simile proper - though we must keep in mind the multiple disturbances in the position of simile particles in Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX as disc. passim above.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two vss. contain forms of kav├н-. The epithet тАЬwide-goingтАЭ (urug─Бy├б13c) may be further specified in the phrase vim─Б╠Бno r├бjasaс╕е тАЬmeasurer of the airy realmтАЭ (14b) – in both cases probably a way of giving a cosmic dimension to the journey across the filter. The third vs. (15) does not participate in these commonalities.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey attach him by seven ceremonies to the three-backed three-benched chariot of the с╣Ыс╣гis to go to the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seven ceremonies: The back are the three oblations, the benches are the three vedas, and the ceremonies are the seven hymns, ch─Бndas

Jamison Brereton

They yoke him to the three-backed, three-seated chariot, to drive, yoking him by means of the seven visionary thoughts of the seven seers.

Jamison Brereton Notes

See published introduction. for the ritual specificity of the images in this vs. The participle тАЬyokingтАЭ in the published translation of c should properly be in parens., since itтАЩs simply generated from the finite yu├▒janti in b.

The uninflected numeral тАШsevenтАЩ (sapt├б) is stationed between two pl. nouns, gen. с╣Ы╠Бс╣г─лс╣З─Бс╣Г тАШof the seersтАЩ and instr. dh─лt├нbhiс╕е тАШwith visionary thoughtsтАЩ. Of course seven is the canonical number of seers throughout Indian religious history, starting with the RV, but тАШsevenтАЩ is also used of dh─лt├н- in IX.9.4 s├б sapt├б dh─лt├нbhir hit├бс╕е and passages cited there. Most tr. choose to construe it with one or the other (Geldner, Ober [II.72] с╣Ы╠Бс╣гi-; Renou, L├╝ders [710], Ober [II.222] dh─лt├н-), with, surprisingly (to me), more going for dh─лt├н- than с╣Ы╠Бс╣гi-. But surely its position helps signal that it should be construed with both (as Renou in his n. and Ober in his 2nd tr. indicate).

That he may move, they yoke him to the three-backed triple-seated car
By the Seven Rsis’ holy songs.

Dem Wagen, der drei R├╝cken hat, drei Sitze, schirren sie ihn an Zur Fahrt durch sieben S├дngerwerk.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is notable for its 2nd ps. address to the priests (sot─Бraс╕е тАж hinota тАЬo pressers, impel тАжтАЭ), also found in vss. 21, 29. Ordinarily 2nd ps. in soma hymns is reserved for Soma (sg.) and his drops (etc.) (pl.).

English translation:

тАЬThe devout priests milk forth your sweet juice Indu, for the gods for the purpose of exhilaration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The ─Аyus milk your milk for exhilaration, o drop;
the gods (milk) honey for the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner and Renou, the published translation interpr. p├бyo duhanti as тАЬthey milk your milkтАЭ (or more emphatically, Renou тАЬtraient de toi le laitтАЭ [my ital.]); that is, they assume that milk (p├бyaс╕е) here refers to the soma juice. See above, comm. ad vs. 9, on the ambiguous ref. of this word in the soma maс╣Зс╕Нala. It is also possible here that p├бyaс╕е refers to cowsтАЩ milk (see the cows in 19c), and the passage should be interpr. тАЬthey milk milk for you for exhilaration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

There is some chaining between vss. (cows/milk in 19, 20; m├бdhu in 20, 21 and two mentions of gods in p─Бda c in 20, 21, incl. dat. pl. dev├йbhyaс╕е in each). In addition, all three vss. begin with the preverb ─Б╠Б(univerbated and therefore accentless in 19a).

Griffith

Indu, the living men milk out the juice to make the rapturous draught:
Gods for the Gods milk out the meath.

Deine Milch, o Saft, melken die Ayu┬┤s zum Rauschtrank, die G├╢tter f├╝r die G├╢tter die S├╝├Яigkeit.

There is some chaining between vss. (cows/milk in 19, 20; m├бdhu in 20, 21 and two mentions of gods in p─Бda c in 20, 21, incl. dat. pl. dev├йbhyaс╕е in each). In addition, all three vss. begin with the preverb ─Б╠Б(univerbated and therefore accentless in 19a).

Jamison Brereton

And rush to all our refreshments provided with cows, encircled with rhythm,
while being hymned by Jamadagni.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For some disc. of this passage see Scarlatta 641 with n. 906. He gives pariс╣гс╣н├║bh- an active value (тАЬringsum jubelnd, rauschendтАЭ) in this passage: тАЬтАж zu allen, die ringsum T├╢ne von sich geben,тАЭ in contrast to my passive тАЬencircled with rhythm,тАЭ which follows RenouтАЩs тАЬenvironn├йes de rhythmes.тАЭ Since the cmpd modifies ├нс╣гaс╕е тАШrefreshmentsтАЩ, it is hard to see how they could actively produce noise, though Scarlatta (n. 906) suggests it might refer to the cows likewise characterizing the refreshments (g├│mat─лr ├нс╣гaс╕е), in the form of bellowing milk streams. This seems a bit farfetched, though it does allow the form to be semantically united with its other occurrence, in I.166.11, where it modifies the Maruts, who are actively making noise. For the idiom see I.80.9 p├бri с╣гс╣нobhata тАЬencircle (him) with rhythm!тАЭ where it is parallel to arcata тАЬchant!тАЭ See also nearby IX.64.28 pariс╣гс╣н├│bhant-. Geldner takes pariс╣гс╣нubhaс╕е as a noun тАШlauter LobliederтАЩ, also with active sense.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Because of the accentual difference between v─Бc├бс╕е in 25a and v─Б╠Бcaс╕е in 26b, we must construe the two superficially near-identical phrases v─Бc├│ agriy├бс╕е and agriy├│ v─Б╠Бcaс╕е quite differently. The first is a single constituent with dependent gen. v─Бc├бс╕е, but in the 2nd agriy├бс╕е and acc pl. v─Б╠Бcaс╕е belong to different constituents, despite their adjacency: v─Б╠Бcaс╕е is the (or rather, an) obj. of ─лr├бyan.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca shows more signs of unity than others in this hymn, esp. in the 1st two vss. Both 25 and 26 contain p─Бda-initial p├бvasva (25a, 26c) and the variant phrases v─Бc├│ agriy├бс╕е (25a) / agriy├│ v─Б╠Бcaс╕е (26b), as well as forms of v├н┼Ыva- (25c v├н┼Ыv─Бni, 26c vi┼Ыvam(ejaya)). In 27a Soma is addressed by the voc. kave, while 25c contains the phrase v├н┼Ыv─Бni k─Б╠Бvy─Б.

This tс╣Ыca shows more signs of unity than others in this hymn, esp. in the 1st two vss. Both 25 and 26 contain p─Бda-initial p├бvasva (25a, 26c) and the variant phrases v─Бc├│ agriy├бс╕е (25a) / agriy├│ v─Б╠Бcaс╕е (26b), as well as forms of v├н┼Ыva- (25c v├н┼Ыv─Бni, 26c vi┼Ыvam(ejaya)). Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPurify for Indra the fierce Indu, the means of strength, the lord (of wealth), the giver of riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For Indra purify the drop, the strong one bringing success to skill, the lord whose largesse is worth pursuing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although it may not be clear from the Engl. tr., the phrase beginning тАЬthe strong one тАж the lordтАЭ refer to Soma (in the acc.), not Indra (in the dat.).

тАЬThe truthful seer, Pavama─Бna Soma, sits down upon the filter, giving great energy to the worshipper.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Self-purifying Soma, the entruthed poet, has sat in the filter,
establishing for the praiser an abundance of heroes.
